SUBENT        14521001   20240403                             15111452100100001 
BIB                 14        168                                 1452100100002 
TITLE      The Baghdad atlas: A relational database of inelastic  1452100100003 
           neutron-scattering (n,n'gamma) data                    1452100100004 
AUTHOR     (A.M.Hurst,L.A.Bernstein,T.Kawano,A.M.Lewis,K.Song)    1452100100005 
REFERENCE  (J,NIM/A,995,165095,2021) Journal publication for data 1452100100006 
           re-analysis and database.                              1452100100007 
           #doi:10.1016/j.nima.2021.165095                        1452100100008 
           (R,LBNL-1007259,2017) Re-analysis of                   1452100100009 
           Baghdad data. This report is relevant to all           1452100100010 
           subentries, as it presents a detailed description of   1452100100011 
           the methods by which the analysis to extract these     1452100100012 
           cross-sections was performed.                          1452100100013 
REL-REF    (N,,A.M.Demidov+,B,GAMMAATLAS,,,1978)=                 1452100100014 
           (N,,A.M.Demidov+,R,INDC(CCP)-120,1978)                 1452100100015 
            Original Gammaatlas                                   1452100100016 
INSTITUTE  (1USAUCX,1USABRK,1USALAS)                              1452100100017 
           (1USAUSA) Naval Nuclear Laboratory, Schenectady, USA   1452100100018 
FACILITY   (REAC,3IRQNRI)  Reactor IRT-5000, in Baghdad.          1452100100019 
INC-SOURCE (REAC) A flux-average neutron energy of approximately  1452100100020 
           1.17 MeV.                                              1452100100021 
INC-SPECT  The data was taken in a broad, fast IRT-5000 reactor   1452100100022 
           spectrum that was filtered to remove thermal           1452100100023 
           contributions. The authors characterized the spectrum  1452100100024 
           as being monotonically decreasing with increasing      1452100100025 
           neutron energy, and the spectrum can be described      1452100100026 
           approximately by a flux distribution phi(En) ~= exp(-  1452100100027 
           0.7473 En) for neutron energies above 2 MeV, ranging   1452100100028 
           from 0.5 - 10 MeV, with a flux-average neutron energy  1452100100029 
           of approximately 1.17 MeV, as shown on page 14, figure 1452100100030 
           5 of this work [1978DE41].                             1452100100031 
DETECTOR   (GELI) Energy and efficiency calibrations of the 30    1452100100032 
           cm**3 Ge(Li) spectrometer were performed using a       1452100100033 
           variety of standard radioactive sources (75Se, 182Ta,  1452100100034 
           110Ag, 72Ga, 140La, 24Na, and 134Cs) and an additional 1452100100035 
           reaction source (14-SI-28(N,G)14-SI-29) for energies   1452100100036 
           below and above 3 MeV, respectively, using state-of-   1452100100037 
           the-art values for these sources as of 1978.           1452100100038 
           Corrections are also made for gamma-ray self absorption1452100100039 
           within the samples. This single detector at 90 degrees 1452100100040 
           was used for most experiments, with the measurements on1452100100041 
           chlorine (subentry 14521014), scandium (14521017),     1452100100042 
           bromine (14521031), lutetium (14521089), osmium        1452100100043 
            (14521097), iridium (14521098), and tellurium         1452100100044 
            (subentries 14521061 -- 14521065) instead using a     1452100100045 
           higher-resolution 40 cm**3 Ge(Li) spectrometer,        1452100100046 
           calibrated in the same fashion. The 30 cm**3 detector  1452100100047 
           resolution is quoted as initially being 3.8 keV at 1.2 1452100100048 
           MeV, degrading down to 8 keV over the course of        1452100100049 
           measurements due to radiation damage, and the 40 cm**3 1452100100050 
           detector resolution is quoted as 2 keV at 1.2 MeV.     1452100100051 
           Background spectra for both detectors were measured    1452100100052 
           using samples of graphite and beryllium, with the      1452100100053 
           energies and intensities of all background lines shown 1452100100054 
           on page 25, table 1 of this work [1978DE41]. There is  1452100100055 
           no indication in [1978DE41] that any angular           1452100100056 
           correlation corrections were applied to the gamma-ray  1452100100057 
           intensities.                                           1452100100058 
METHOD     (ACTIV,EXTB,GSPEC) Samples were irradiated using a Cd- 1452100100059 
           filtered reactor neutron spectrum from an IRT-5000     1452100100060 
           reactor based at the Al-Tuwaitha research facility     1452100100061 
           outside of Baghdad, Iraq in the 1970s, as described in 1452100100062 
           INC-SPECT. Gamma-ray intensities were measured using a 1452100100063 
           Ge(Li) detector, as described in DETECTOR, shielded    1452100100064 
           with iron (5 cm), paraffin with boron carbide (8 cm),  1452100100065 
           lead (10 cm), and 6Li (3 mm). Gamma rays passing to the1452100100066 
           detector from the target were filtered from fast       1452100100067 
           neutrons with a 6.8 g/cm**2 layer of lithium hydride   1452100100068 
            (LiH).                                                1452100100069 
MONITOR    (26-FE-56(N,INL)26-FE-56,PAR,SIG,G) All intensities    1452100100070 
           were measured relative to the intensity of the         1452100100071 
           846.8-keV 1st 2+ --> G.S. 0+ gamma-ray transition in   1452100100072 
           56Fe from the Fe-56(n,ng) reaction.                    1452100100073 
ANALYSIS   Using the gamma-ray intensity data (normalized to the  1452100100074 
           846.8-keV transition in 56Fe, as described in MONITOR),1452100100075 
           the partial gamma-ray production cross section is      1452100100076 
           extracted for each observed transition in the Atlas.   1452100100077 
           This normalization is performed in a two-step fashion, 1452100100078 
           where the gamma line with the most reliable intensity  1452100100079 
           measurement is selected for each sample. This reference1452100100080 
           line (identified in ANALYSIS for the subentry of each  1452100100081 
           sample) is in turn normalized to the 846.8-keV line in 1452100100082 
           56Fe (described in MONITOR) using data from Table 2,   1452100100083 
           p.25-27 in [1978DE41], where the relative intensity of 1452100100084 
           the 846.8-keV line in 56Fe is defined to be 100%. All  1452100100085 
           other lines belonging to each sample nucleus are in    1452100100086 
           turn normalized to their corresponding reference gamma 1452100100087 
           line. The magnitude of each reference line is itself   1452100100088 
           normalized to the flux-weighted                        1452100100089 
            (26-FE-56(N,INL)26-FE-56) cross section for the first 1452100100090 
           2+ state in 56Fe, corresponding to 978.965 +/- 13.430  1452100100091 
           mb. The flux-weighted cross section was determined by  1452100100092 
           convolving the filtered IRT-5000 reactor spectrum (as  1452100100093 
           shown on page 14, figure 5 of this work [1978DE41])    1452100100094 
           with the ENDF/B-VIII.0 value for the                   1452100100095 
            (26-FE-56(N,INL)26-FE-56) cross section to the first  1452100100096 
           2+ state. This cross section includes direct feeding of1452100100097 
           the first 2+ state in 56Fe (MT=51), as well as feeding 1452100100098 
           via the discrete excited states of 56Fe                1452100100099 
            (MT=52-56,58,60,63,68,70,72,73,78,82) and a 58%       1452100100100 
           feeding contribution from the continuum (MT=91). The   1452100100101 
           continuum contribution is an estimate based on the     1452100100102 
           observed feeding from discrete states relative to the  1452100100103 
           cross-section summation from direct and discrete-level 1452100100104 
           feeding contributions. Excitation energies (E-EXC),    1452100100105 
           gamma-ray energies (E-GAMMA), and branching ratios (BR)1452100100106 
           are taken from, or deduced using information in, ENSDF.1452100100107 
           These are summarized in a table below. A small         1452100100108 
           correction (98.85(3)% branching ratio) corresponding to1452100100109 
           the beta minus decay of 56Mn formed in the             1452100100110 
            (26-FE-56(N,P)25-MN-56) reaction (0.91613(28) mb) has 1452100100111 
           been accounted for in the determination of the flux-   1452100100112 
           weighted cross section. No neutron-gamma angular       1452100100113 
           correlation corrections appear to have been performed  1452100100114 
           by the authors of [1978DE41].                          1452100100115 
           ----------------------------------------------------   1452100100116 
           File   E-EXC (keV)   E-GAMMA (keV)      BR             1452100100117 
           ----------------------------------------------------   1452100100118 
           MT51    846.8          846.8           1.0             1452100100119 
           MT52    2085.1         1238.3          1.00(2)         1452100100120 
           MT53    2657.6         1810.8          0.970(5)        1452100100121 
           MT54    2941.5         2094.9          1.0             1452100100122 
           MT55    2960.0         2113.1          0.978(27)       1452100100123 
           MT56    3120.1         2273.2          0.954(9)        1452100100124 
           MT58    3370.0         2523.1          0.855(12)       1452100100125 
           MT60    3445.3         2598.5          0.785(3)        1452100100126 
           MT63    3605.7         2759.0          0.583(38)       1452100100127 
           MT68    3830.0         2983.0          0.518(66)       1452100100128 
           MT70    4048.9         3202.0          0.808(4)        1452100100129 
           MT72    4100.4         3253.5          0.622(4)        1452100100130 
           MT73    4119.9         3273.1          0.187(1)        1452100100131 
           MT78    4394.9         3548.1          0.907(10)       1452100100132 
           MT82    4509.6         3662.7          0.314(65)       1452100100133

ERR-ANALYS (ERR-T) The total uncertainties of the measurements    1452100100136 
           were calculated according to Gaussian error            1452100100137 
           propagation.                                           1452100100138 
           (MONIT-ERR) The total uncertainty in the               1452100100139 
            (26-FE-56(N,INL)26-FE-56) cross section to the first  1452100100140 
           2+ state in 56Fe (MT=51). Includes Gaussian propagated 1452100100141 
           contributions due to branching-ratio uncertainties     1452100100142 
           corresponding to the feeding of the 1st 2+ state in    1452100100143 
           56Fe from discrete excited states                      1452100100144 
            (MT=52-56,58,60,63,68,70,72,73,78,82), and an         1452100100145 
           estimated 50% uncertainty in the assumed branching     1452100100146 
           ratio for the continuum (MT=91) feeding contribution,  1452100100147 
           as described in ANALYSIS. An additional correction is  1452100100148 
           made for the population of the 846.8 keV transition    1452100100149 
           from the decay of 56Mn produced in the 56Fe(n,p)       1452100100150 
           reaction channel.                                      1452100100151 
           (ERR-1) Relative gamma-ray transition intensity.       1452100100152 
           Uncertainty includes statistical error (with 95%       1452100100153 
           probability) folded with uncertainties due to the      1452100100154 
           spectrometer efficiency, as described in DETECTOR, and 1452100100155 
           a gamma-ray self-absorption term.                      1452100100156 
           (ERR-2) Normalization factor for determination of      1452100100157 
           absolute partial gamma-ray cross sections. Uncertainty 1452100100158 
           includes a statistical error (with 95% probability)    1452100100159 
           folded with uncertainties due to efficiency            1452100100160 
           determination of spectrometer, as described in         1452100100161 
           DETECTOR, and gamma-ray self-absorption.               1452100100162 
           (E-ERR) Total uncertainty in gamma-ray energy,         1452100100163 
           including statistics errors (with 95% probability),    1452100100164 
           errors due to calibration, and non-linearity of the    1452100100165 
           spectroscopic tract for Egamma.                        1452100100166
